e8mq1e910">BBC News, Myanmar</div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-jlwt2c-Divider e8mq1e915"></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><b class="ssrcss-1xjjfut-BoldText e5tfeyi3">Two loudspeakers, as big as the men carrying them, are brought to the rocky hilltop. Some 800m below, in the town of Hpasang, lies a sprawling Myanmar army base.</b></p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Its a blisteringly hot day - above 40C - and behind, on bamboo poles, more young resistance fighters carry a large, heavy battery pack and amplifier. Leading the ascent is Nay Myo Zin, a former army captain who, after 12 years in the military, defected to the resistance.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">With his dark green camouflage jacket draped over one shoulder, he has the air of a performer about to take the stage. He is here to urge the soldiers in the base below, who are loyal to the countrys ruling military, to switch sides.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div browser.</h2></div></div></noscript></div></div><figcaption class="ssrcss-1mget3o-StyledFigureCaption e34k3c22"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Media caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-y7krbn-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;Ceasefire! Ceasefire!&quot; - Nay Myo Zin bellows his plea to the army base</p></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-5rhf4g-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In this jungle deep in Karenni state in the east of Myanmar, two forces face each other in a fight that has, in one way or another, been going on for decades. But the rapid advances by the resistance in recent months indicate that this time they may have the advantage.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The South East Asian nation is at a crossroads - after decades of military rule and brutal repression, ethnic groups, along with a new army of young insurgents, have brought the dictatorship to crisis point.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In the past seven months, somewhere between half and two-thirds of the country has fallen to the resistance. Tens of thousands of people have been killed, including many children, since the military seized power in a coup in 2021. Some 2.5 million have been displaced, and the military facing an unprecedented challenge to its rule and in an attempt to thwart the growing resistance regularly bombs civilians, schools and churches from its warplanes (the resistance has none).</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="image-block" class="ssrcss-1pyuwv1-ComponentWrapper ep2nwvo1"><figure class="ssrcss-8589xk-StyledFigure e34k3c23"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-1jlpy5h-Placeholder etlorgc0"><span><noscript><picture><source srcSet="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/240/cpsprodpb/96e5/live/5791f210-181f-11ef-b5cc-cb8b8c4cef5a.png.webp 240w, 976w" width="1024" height="1070.4" class="ssrcss-11yxrdo-Image edrdn950"/></picture></noscript></span></span></div></figure></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-5rhf4g-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Before Nay Myo Zins sound equipment is switched on, the army opens fire on his position.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Undeterred, with a flick of the switch and microphone in hand, he bellows: Everyone, cease fire! Cease fire, please. Just listen for five minutes, 10 minutes. Somewhat surprisingly, the barrage stops.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">He tells them of the 4,000 soldiers who surrendered to the opposition in northern Shan State, and the recent insurgent drone attacks on military buildings in the countrys capital Nay Pyi Taw. The message is, we are winning, your regime is falling, it is time to give up.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Here in Hpasang and across Karenni state, across much of the country, battles and stalemates have taken hold as a great rolling rebellion threatens the rule of the military junta. The military coup in 2021 brought an end to the elected civilian government, and its leader Aung San Suu Kyi remains imprisoned, along with other political leaders.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Yet this is an under-reported conflict - with much of the worlds attention on Ukraine and the Israel-Gaza conflict. There is no press freedom, foreign journalists are rarely allowed to enter officially and when they do are heavily monitored. There is no way to hear the resistance side of this story through government approved visits.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">We travelled into Myanmar and spent a month in the east of the country living alongside resistance groups fighting across Karenni State, which borders Thailand, and Shan state, which borders China.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">We travelled on jungle tracks and backroads, to front lines where the military has been cut off and surrounded for weeks, where like in Hpasang, the fighters have the high ground. In others, such as Moebye, further north, the opposition has suffered heavy losses as it attempted direct assaults across heavily mined ground. There, and in Loikaw, the state capital, the strength of the rebellion and its limitations are in plain view.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="image-block" class="ssrcss-1pyuwv1-ComponentWrapper ep2nwvo1"><figure class="ssrcss-8589xk-StyledFigure e34k3c23"><div https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/800/cpsprodpb/027c/live/4fdb5c90-1140-11ef-b9d8-4f52aebe147d.jpg.webp 800w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/976/cpsprodpb/027c/live/4fdb5c90-1140-11ef-b9d8-4f52aebe147d.jpg.webp 976w" type="image/webp"/><img alt=" Nay Myo Zin broadcasts to the camp below" loading="lazy" src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/1536/cpsprodpb/027c/live/4fdb5c90-1140-11ef-b9d8-4f52aebe147d.jpg" srcSet="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/240/cpsprodpb/027c/live/4fdb5c90-1140-11ef-b9d8-4f52aebe147d.jpg 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/320/cpsprodpb/027c/live/4fdb5c90-1140-11ef-b9d8-4f52aebe147d.jpg 320w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/480/cpsprodpb/027c/live/4fdb5c90-1140-11ef-b9d8-4f52aebe147d.jpg 976w" width="1536" height="1024" class="ssrcss-11yxrdo-Image edrdn950"/></picture></noscript></span></span></div><figcaption class="ssrcss-1mget3o-StyledFigureCaption e34k3c22"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-y7krbn-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Nay Myo Zin broadcasts to the camp below</p></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-5rhf4g-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In Hpasang, the resistance has been playing a waiting game, confident that they have the upper hand. Some 80 soldiers have been trapped inside the base for more than a month, with about 100 more believed to be dead or injured.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Up on the hilltop, via his loudspeaker, Nay Myo Zin makes the case for surrender: We have surrounded you. There is no possibility of a helicopter coming. Ground troops support? No. You have time today to decide whether to switch to the peoples side.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Theres silence from the military camp below.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Nay Myo Zin urges them to abandon Min Aung Hlaing, the general in charge of the ruling junta.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">All your lives will surely be spared. This is the highest promise that I can give. So, dont be foolish. Would you rather protect tyrant Min Aung Hlaings unjustifiable wealth until your last breath? Now, I am waiting to welcome you.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Moments pass, there is only the sound of flies buzzing on the hilltop, as perhaps the junta forces are considering their response. It is no easy decision, if they surrender and are returned to military-controlled areas, they will probably be sentenced to death.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Their answer comes loudly; definitively. They again fire on the rocky outpost, the insurgents begin to duck for cover. There will be no surrender today.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Nay Myo Zin continues broadcasting, regardless. To his side, on a radio, the commander of the operation to capture the base adopts a different approach. On the same frequency as the military men, he exchanges insults with them.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In an onslaught of slurs, he accuses them of being Min Aung Hlaings guard dogs, and of being unfaithful to their country.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The soldiers respond with insults of their own. Cut off from the resupply of men and food, they stand their ground, firm in their belief that it is the militarys right - its destiny - to rule the country.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The ideological gulf between both sides is unbridgeable.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The carrot and stick approach continues for another 30 minutes or so, before the resistance fighters withdraw. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In his enthusiastic appeal for surrender Nay Myo Zin has inadvertently given away the mens position (Im 400 yards away beside the loudspeakers, he said), and they are worried about an artillery or mortar strike. Later that evening, the hillside takes a direct hit, without injuries.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="image-block" class="ssrcss-1pyuwv1-ComponentWrapper ep2nwvo1"><figure class="ssrcss-8589xk-StyledFigure e34k3c23"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-1govoti-Placeholder etlorgc0"><span><noscript><picture><source srcSet="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/240/cpsprodpb/1de9/live/b2394f90-16a5-11ef-a5f9-c9e97f2e93cf.png.webp 976w" width="999" height="99.9" class="ssrcss-11yxrdo-Image edrdn950"/></picture></noscript></span></span></div></figure></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-5rhf4g-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">This is more than just an ideological battle, it is a generational war. The young against the establishment, a new order fighting to break free from a tenacious old order. The connected versus a disconnected elite. The same youth who heard tales of failed revolutions and who have decided now is their time.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">After half a century of military rule, Myanmar enjoyed a brief experiment with democracy starting in 2015 under Suu Kyi and her National League for Democracy.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">For many young people those years, though not without deep problems, marked an all-too-short golden age of freedom. The ballot box had failed them, then peaceful protest in the wake of the coup was met with killings and arrests. Many of those fighting told us there had been no alternative but to take up arms.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Thousands have abandoned studies and careers in major cities such as Yangon - doctors, mathematicians, martial arts fighters - and fled the cities to join established ethnic and resistance groups that had long opposed military rule.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">On this front, all the fighters are under 25.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="image-block" class="ssrcss-1pyuwv1-ComponentWrapper ep2nwvo1"><figure class="ssrcss-8589xk-StyledFigure e34k3c23"><div 976w" width="2048" height="1152" class="ssrcss-11yxrdo-Image edrdn950"/></picture></noscript></span></span></div><figcaption class="ssrcss-1mget3o-StyledFigureCaption e34k3c22"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-y7krbn-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Nam Ree aims a sniper rifle towards the enemy position</p></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-5rhf4g-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Nam Ree, a 22-year-old with the Karenni Nationalities Defence Force, KNDF, explains why he joined the resistance.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The dogs [a commonly used insult for the military] have been unjust. They carried out an unlawful military coup. We, the youth, are discontented with it, he says.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">He is wearing flip flops, blue nail varnish, faded combat trousers and ammo belt across a Barcelona FC top. Unlike most of the men around him, he has a ballistic helmet. No-one has body armour.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The KNDF are a new force of young fighters and commanders which appeared after the coup. Ethnic armed groups have been fighting against the military in Karenni - also known as Kayah state - for decades. But the KNDF has brought them unity and battlefield success.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The tide turned against the junta on 27 October last year when an alliance of groups in the north of the country overran military positions and border crossings. Dozens more towns across the country have fallen since then into the hands of the armed opposition. The military still controls the main cities, but is losing control of the countryside and Myanmars borders.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The KNDF says it, and other insurgent groups, now control 90% of the Karenni state. It may be the smallest in the country but it has become a hardcore centre of resistance.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="image-block" class="ssrcss-1pyuwv1-ComponentWrapper ep2nwvo1"><figure class="ssrcss-8589xk-StyledFigure e34k3c23"><div 976w" width="1536" height="1024" class="ssrcss-11yxrdo-Image edrdn950"/></picture></noscript></span></span></div><figcaption class="ssrcss-1mget3o-StyledFigureCaption e34k3c22"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-y7krbn-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Deputy commander, Maui Pho Thaike</p></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-5rhf4g-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Under the shade of a mango orchard sits the powerfully built, tattooed KNDF deputy commander, Maui Pho Thaike. An environmentalist who studied in the United States, he first picked up a gun three years ago.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">He doesnt recognise the military junta as a government, it is the oppressor of the countrys many ethnic regions, he says.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">He says the whole country is now fighting the army.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The strategies are changing. All the attacks are now co-ordinated, he says.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The KNDF has no lack of fighters, but ammunition and weapons are in desperately short supply. Mostly the insurgency is funded by donations from the countrys diaspora.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">We do have enough heart, we do have enough morale, we do have enough humanity. That&#x27;s the way we&#x27;re going to defeat them, Maui says.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">A tattoo on his hand reads free thinker - from another time, when Myanmar was briefly on its thwarted move to democracy. Are you still a free thinker, I ask him. In this uniform, no, he replies. But without this uniform, Im a free man. And thats our dream. Well create it again.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="image-block" class="ssrcss-1pyuwv1-ComponentWrapper ep2nwvo1"><figure class="ssrcss-8589xk-StyledFigure e34k3c23"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-n0t9s-Placeholder etlorgc0"><span><noscript><picture><source srcSet="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/240/cpsprodpb/f7e6/live/d251f3a0-1140-11ef-82e8-cd354766a224.jpg.webp 240w, class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-y7krbn-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Maui Pho Thaike trains KNDF fighters</p></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-5rhf4g-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">To enter Myanmar is to travel not just to a forgotten war, but to country severed from the outside world. Much of the mobile phone network, internet and electricity has been cut off in Karenni state. The military may be on the back foot but their remaining bases control the main roads through the state.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">A 60km (37 mile) drive from Hpasang further north to the town of Demoso took more than 10 hours across rutted dirt tracks, over hills and through rivers and valleys.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">We arrived to the aftermath of a failed assault on a military base in the nearby town of Moebye, in which 27 members of the resistance had been killed.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In a jungle hospital, young men from the KNDF lie on hospital beds on dirt floors. Some smile and give a thumbs up, most are missing limbs.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="image-block" class="ssrcss-1pyuwv1-ComponentWrapper ep2nwvo1"><figure class="ssrcss-8589xk-StyledFigure e34k3c23"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-n0t9s-Placeholder etlorgc0"><span><noscript><picture><source srcSet="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/240/cpsprodpb/ea2d/live/c62b99a0-1140-11ef-bee9-6125e244a4cd.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/news/976/cpsprodpb/ea2d/live/c62b99a0-1140-11ef-bee9-6125e244a4cd.jpg.webp 976w" type="image/webp"/><img alt="Aung Ngle" loading="lazy" 976w" width="1536" height="1024" class="ssrcss-11yxrdo-Image edrdn950"/></picture></noscript></span></span></div><figcaption class="ssrcss-1mget3o-StyledFigureCaption e34k3c22"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-y7krbn-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Aung Ngle has a swollen leg</p></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-5rhf4g-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Aung Ngle, 23, has a horribly swollen left leg after taking shrapnel to his femoral artery in the attack on the base. He is too ill to talk, but as he begins to weep, three of his comrades come to him, holding and comforting him. They wont be able to operate. He will have to make the long journey to Thailand for further treatment. I ask a doctor if he will survive. He will be fine, he says. But right now I think hes depressed because he cant fight anymore.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In many respects, this is a conflict from another age, brutal and intimate. The fighting in Moebye lasted for days, at close quarters, with uphill frontal infantry assaults on the militarys bunkers.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">One man has multiple injuries to his hands, legs and stomach. They were caused by a hand grenade, he says. They had gone to retrieve a commander who had been hit in the leg when it came in. It was at close range - about 30ft, he says.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The war has a slow ferocity, as we saw for ourselves when we travelled further north into southern Shan state, towards the town of Hsihseng. Near there, a counter-offensive was underway as the military tried to capture the route to Loikaw, the state capital, which also remains contested.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">It is not their state, but the KNDF is in the lead under the command of a fighter called Darthawr. He, like many of his men, has been injured in previous attacks and a dark red scar peeks out from under the arm of his T-shirt.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Defending this place for us is like defending our home, he tells me. He is in shorts and flip flops and neither he nor his men have body armour. Nor do we.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">As we stand on a low hilltop by a banana grove, he points out the militarys positions, 1.5km (0.9 miles) away. Shells begin landing nearby and there is a scramble to some shallow trenches. The shells, likely mortars, keep coming in, getting closer. A sustained exchange of automatic gunfire can be heard at close range - it sounds like the soldiers are far closer than previously thought.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">It quickly becomes apparent that a group of soldiers is making its way through a minefield to our position. We leave, driving at speed as the shelling continues, a mortar striking the road directly ahead of the vehicles.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Their troops got injured, and thats why they are randomly shooting everywhere, Darthawr explained.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div 976w" width="999" height="99.9" class="ssrcss-11yxrdo-Image edrdn950"/></picture></noscript></span></span></div></figure></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-5rhf4g-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">At a graduation ceremony on a baked-hard dirt parade ground cleared in the jungle, rank after rank of new recruits march past in formation. They salute the KNDF leadership, their rubber-soled canvas boots stamping up the dust. The young men and women - many just turned 18 - march to the beat of a song in English, Warrior. Its lyrics:</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><i class="ssrcss-xbdn93-ItalicText e5tfeyi2">I am last to leave, but the first to go</i></p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><i class="ssrcss-xbdn93-ItalicText e5tfeyi2">Lord, make me dead before you make me old</i></p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><i class="ssrcss-xbdn93-ItalicText e5tfeyi2">I am a Soldier and I&#x27;m marching on</i></p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><i class="ssrcss-xbdn93-ItalicText e5tfeyi2">I am a warrior and this is my song</i></p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">There are more than 500 - a record number of recruits. The ranks have been swollen after the junta, running short of men, enacted a conscription decree which sent young people in their hundreds fleeing to insurgent territory to join the revolutionary cause.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="image-block" 976w" width="2048" height="1152" class="ssrcss-11yxrdo-Image edrdn950"/></picture></noscript></span></span></div><figcaption class="ssrcss-1mget3o-StyledFigureCaption e34k3c22"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-y7krbn-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">KNDF graduation ceremony</p></div></figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-5rhf4g-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The last time I saw the troops, they were training with bamboo rifles. Now they have the real thing.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Their commander, Maui tells me that there isnt much time for training. Our strategy is like, we organised one month training, intensive training, then we go to fight.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">As the ceremony ends the mood is wild. A young rapper, MC Kayar Lay, who also graduated that day sends the fresh recruits into a frenzy of dancing and celebration.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">It is difficult to predict where the uprising will lead. For both sides, this is an existential war and one increasingly marked by bloodshed and bitterness. There appears to be no going back.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">After three and a half weeks, we were back in Hpasang. The army base, which had been about to be stormed by the resistance when I left, remained standing.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The military had tried to send in reinforcements - some 100 men - but in a battle with the insurgents, 57 were captured, the rest fled or were killed.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The army failed to resupply the base but the encounter with the opposition forces had another consequence. It meant armed revolutionaries&#x27; ammunition was depleted - and they no longer were able mount an attack on the outpost.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The day before we arrived, army war planes had bombed the hilltop overlooking Hpasang, killing three of the young fighters we had met earlier, and injuring 10. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Before, there had been music and singing from their positions on the banks of the wide Salween River, an almost relaxed willingness to wait out their enemy. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">But now the mood had darkened - more appeals for surrender seemed unlikely. It would now be a battle to the death.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="ssrcss-1ocoo3l-Wrap e42f8511"><div width="wide" class="ssrcss-ahx90r-WrapWithWidth e42f8510"><div
